143. Ibid., Oct. 20, 1926.

Baird died, he left several hundred dollars to establish the Baird Foundation. It was his intention that his small bequest should be left untouched for 300 years, or until it should grow to twenty-four quadrillion dollars, and he provided that the interest on that sum should be used to relieve the citizens of Boulder from paying general municipal and school taxes, and to provide many improvements, such as a hospital, a library, a symphony orchestra, an art museum, and park lands.<sup>144</sup> Thanks to this very far-sighted plan, the citizens of Boulder may look forward to that day 300 years hence when their municipal officers will enjoy considerable relief from their perennial troubles.

144. Ibid., Feb. 2, 1934; interview with Eben G. Fine, vice-president of the trustees of the Baird Foundation, August 18, 1946.



### IN CONCLUSION

Since 1871 the people of Boulder have been employing municipal organization to serve their needs. At first the spare-time attention of seven men sufficed; by 1946 the city was dependent upon the services of more than fifteen volunteers and seventy-some employes. Where once there had been no property or equipment, in 1946 the city had capital assets valued at more than three million dollars.

In the years of noteworthy development the evolution of the city government was influenced by the same forces which shaped the growth of Boulder--diverse natural advantages and the resultant interplay of forces. The municipality has responded especially to two of the factors--the geographic assets and the presence of the University. The University in particular has exercised considerable influence in recent years, through the relationship required by the existence of its expanding physical plant, through the civic consciousness of the need for a wholesome environment for students, and through the influence of many faculty members who have participated in municipal affairs. There was one period in which the trend of municipal management swung briefly towards liberalism, bordering on socialism; but all through the preceding and succeeding eras the administrative policies generally have been conservative.

In the long course of local municipal development certain achievements have been outstanding, namely: the

enviable record of the early volunteer fire companies; the development of an extensive mountain water system and the excellence of its product; the acquisition and improvement of a remarkable system of city and mountain parks; the relatively early paving of nearly all principal streets; the early and long sustained consensus for prohibition; the generally good order in the community maintained by a police force employing half the number of officers generally recommended; the fruitful use of relief labor during the depression; the extraordinary success of a meagerly supported recreation program; the early trial and proved effectiveness of the Hare system of voting; and finally, the general success and popularity of the city manager form of government. With this record as a foundation, the future holds promise of even greater attainments for the City of Boulder.

\* \* \* \* \*

Seek not beyond; the happy shores

Bend nearer here than other where  
 The gifts that wait beside your doors,  
 And on the hills and in the air,  
 Are better than all old conceits,  
 All faded and forgotten sweets.

I see the new Arcana rise

Touched with the fire of other days,

And Nature, grown more rich and wise,

Yield to your prayers her mysteries.

Straight be your furrow, look not back,

Trust that the harvest shall not lack.

Build yet, the end is not; build on,

Build for the ages, unafraid;

The past is but a base whereon

These ashlar, well hewn, may be laid.

Lo, I declare, I deem him best

Whose foot, here pausing, findeth rest.

--By J. Harrison Mills, in History of  
Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, pages  
15-16.



## A P P E N D I X CONDENSED BIOGRAPHIES\*

GUY A. ADAMS  
1859-1933

A native of Iowa, he came to Colorado in 1875, but returned to Pennsylvania for his education in the public schools and at Waynesburg College. In 1892 he became associated with his father in the practice of law at Boulder.

He was a Mason, a Woodman, a member of the Y.M.C.A. board, and member of the board of the Methodist church.

He was first elected to the city council in 1903 (to 1905), and was reelected by the Prohibitionists, 1907-1909. In 1922 he was returned to the city council, from which he resigned in 1929 to become police magistrate. In addition he was a justice of the peace and for four years a deputy county clerk.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Sept. 21, 1933; Minutes of the City Council, 1903-1933).

ANTHONY ARNETT  
1819-1903

A native of Reichstoffs in Alsace-Lorraine, France, he came to the United States in 1828, settling first in Pennsylvania and later in Illinois. He took part in the California gold rush in 1849, and after returning to Illinois

\*The subjects are principally those included in the "honor roll" at the end of Chapter II.

in 1851, participated in another gold rush, in 1859, to Colorado, where he engaged at first in the cattle and freight business.

After locating at Boulder in 1864 he profited from mining and real estate investments, and gave liberally to the University and other enterprises. He was also a pioneer hotel-keeper, an active participant in county affairs, and one of the builders of the Central City and Black Hawk wagon road.

In 1871 the county commissioners named him one of the first trustees of the Town of Boulder.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 607; Boulder Daily Camera, June 12, 1903; Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1861-1871; Forest Crossen, Anthony Arnett, Empire Builder, 1933).

### EUGENE A. AUSTIN 1849-1927

A native of New York, he served under General Grant in the Civil War, and then came to Colorado in 1867. He located at Boulder in 1872, where he opened a butcher shop and later became vice-president and president of the Boulder Pressed Brick Co.

Republican, and past commander, G.A.R.

Town Trustee, 1876-1877 and 1880-1881; Mayor, 1887-1891; Alderman, 1898-1903.

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, pages 755-6; History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 606).

### L. P. BASS 1881-1920

A resident of Boulder after 1890, he engaged in the photography business and in 1896 began a long and distinguished career as a law enforcement officer. City police officer, 1894-1900 and 1903-1905; marshal, 1900-1901 and 1909-1917; chief of police, 1918 to the time of his death in an automobile accident in 1920.

(News-Herald, March 18, 1920, and April 22, 1925; City Council Minutes, April 6, 1920; Bensel's Boulder County Directory, 1892).

### JAMES O. BILLIG 1875-1937

A native of Iowa, he engaged first in the wholesale grocery business at Boulder in 1902.

Member of the Lions Club, Elks lodge, and Chamber of Commerce, and a director of the Chautauqua Association.

Member of the city council 1918-1920, and Mayor, 1920-1928, during the critical testing period of the city manager form of government.

(Baker, History of Colorado, Volume IV, page 611; Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 15, 1926; City Council Minutes, 1918-1928).

### CHARLES R. BURGER 1891-

A native of Denver, he engaged in mining activities from 1923 to 1929, and since 1929 has been associated with his brother in the real estate and insurance business at Boulder.

Member of the Lions Club, Chamber of Commerce, Masonic lodge, Elks lodge, American Legion, and Methodist Church.

Elected to the city council in 1936 and reelected in 1942 for a term expiring in 1948.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 83; Minutes of the City Council, 1936--)

### ALFRED A. BROOKFIELD 1830-1897

A native of New Jersey, he learned merchandising in partnership with his father, and from 1856 to 1858 was in the grocery business at Nebraska City.

In 1858 he came to Boulder, where he engaged first in prospecting and mining, and later in ranching, near Valmont. ~~From 1865 to 1872 he lived at Ward, but returned to Boulder~~ and became the proprietor of the Colorado House.

He was president of the Boulder City Townsite Company, which was organized in February, 1859, and platted the Original Town.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 614; Bancroft, History of Nevada, Colorado, and Wyoming, (1890), page 576. For Mrs. Emily "Auntie" Brookfield, see Semple, Representative Women of Colorado, 1911, page 227, and the Boulder Daily Camera, Nov. 24, 1909.

### CHARLES M. CAMPBELL 1842-1922

A native of Indiana and a graduate of Indiana University, where he received his B.A. degree in 1859 and M.A. in 1862, he moved to Missouri in 1860 and thence to Kansas, where he studied at the Western Theological Seminary and was ordained in 1864 in the Presbyterian ministry.

In 1864 he located at Boulder, where he led in the building of a Presbyterian church. He was a member of the Woodmen's lodge and was a prominent and active Republican. He was instrumental in the first acquisition of government mountain land for a municipal park.

He served as street commissioner, 1878-1880, Police Magistrate, 1882-3, 1885-7, 1903-4, and city attorney, 1887-8 and 1896 to 1903. In addition he was, at times, county attorney, deputy district attorney, and county Republican chairman.

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, page 232).

### --- IDA M. CAMPBELL 1861-

A native of Iowa, Ida M. Perry was educated in a boarding school at Burlington and taught school for a few years before marrying Scott Campbell, a lawyer, who was a native of Vermont and a graduate of Tufts College at Boston.

In 1904 they moved to Boulder, Colorado, where Mr. Campbell died in 1912.

Mrs. Campbell, while assuming responsibility for the continued education of her three sons, also was active in many civic endeavors. In 1917 she was a delegate representing the Woman's Club in the Charter Convention which drafted the provisions governing the city manager form of government employed in Boulder since that time, and in 1918 she was the first woman elected to serve on the city council. In 1922 she was reelected, serving to 1928.

In addition to her significant work in city government she was one of the founders of the Day Nursery, was an active member of the Presbyterian church, the Woman's Club, and the Daughters of the American Revolution, and has been state president of the P.E.O. sisterhood.

(Minutes of the City Council, 1917-1928; letter from C. M. Campbell, April 23, 1946; interview, April 19, 1946).

### CARL E. CARLSON 1896-

A native of Sweden, he came directly to Boulder in 1924 and for eleven years was an employe of a plumbing and heating company.

Since 1935 he has been superintendent of the city water department, with the exception of 1942 to 1945, when he was engaged in Army engineering and also in construction work at Du Pont's atomic bomb plant.

He is a member of the Elks and Masonic lodges, of the A. F. of L., and of the Rocky Mountain Section of the American Water Works Association.

(Interview, April 18, 1946).

### LOUISE C. CHENEY 1878-

A native of Pueblo, Colorado, she obtained her education in Pueblo and Denver, with specialization in music. In 1900 she married Charles H. Cheney, then bookkeeper at the First National Bank in Boulder, and later cashier and president of the bank, to 1933. He died in 1938.

Mrs. Cheney has been prominent in many civic activities, as a member of the board of the Red Cross, of the Columbia Cemetery Association, and of the former University Hospital. She was president of the Day Nursery Association during the years when the present building was erected. She has also been a member of the Woman's Club and of the Daughters of the American Revolution.

Because of her interest in the out-of-doors and of her wide acquaintance, she was appointed a member of the city park board in 1912. She served on it until 1917, and on the Planning and Parks Commission from 1920 to 1935, including several terms as chairman, and in this capacity she was instrumental in engaging outstanding planning consultants.

From 1941 to 1944 she was social director of Kappa Kappa Gamma at the University of Wyoming.

(Minutes of the City Council 1917-1935; letter from Mrs. Flora S. McHarg, April 24, 1946; interview May 3, 1946).

### OLIVER P. CLARK

A native of Vermont, he came to Boulder in 1895 and became established in the grocery business.

He was a member of the Odd Fellows lodge, and served as city clerk and recorder from 1907 to 1918, when he moved to California and engaged in the real estate business to the time of his death in 1931.

(Boulder Daily Camera, June 11, 1896, and February 24, 1931; Minutes of the City Council, December 3, 1918.

### A. DEAN COLEMAN 1901-

A native of Iowa, he was graduated from Boulder high school in 1918 and studied at the University two years. He spent one year as accountant for the Los Angeles Gas and Electric Co., and since then has been in business at Boulder, lately as proprietor of a gasoline retail and wholesale station.

He is a member of the Masonic and Elks lodges and of the Chamber of Commerce, and is a member of the board of the Christian church.

He was elected Republican state representative in 1936, 1938, and 1940, and has served two terms on the city council, from 1934 to 1946.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Nov. 5, 1946; Minutes of the City Council, 1934-1946).

### L. W. CUMBERFORD 1878-

A native of Missouri, he located in Colorado first at Colorado Springs and in 1902 came to Boulder where he has been engaged since in the tea and coffee business. He is now also vice-president of the National State Bank.

Member of the Chamber of Commerce, Rotary, Elks, and Woodmen, a past director of the Chautauqua Association, and a member of the fish committee of the state Chamber of Commerce.

Mayor, 1928 to 1932, and member of the city council since 1932, term expiring in 1950.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 15, 1926; Minutes of the City Council, 1928 to date; and interview, April 16 1946).

### JOHN A. ELLET 1838-1892

A native of Illinois, he went to California in 1853 to join his father in the hotel business, and in 1858-9 he was enrolled in the University of the Pacific at Santa Clara. After teaching in the public schools he returned to the Midwest for service in the Union Navy.

After the Civil War he was in the mercantile business at Vicksburg and Yazoo City until 1875 when he came to Boulder and engaged in the real estate business.

Republican delegate to the Chicago convention in 1880, a founder of the Boulder Board of Trade, and a charter member of the Boulder Library Association.

Elected president of the town trustees, 1876-1877, and mayor twice, 1880-1881 and 1882-1883.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 634; Boulder Daily Camera, April 13, 1892; and Minutes of the City Council, 1876-1882).

### HERBERT S. EVANS 1875-

A native of Nebraska, and educated at the University of Nebraska and Morrill College, he engaged in electrical engineering work in Nebraska from 1898 to 1901 and then became instructor of electrical engineering at the University of Nebraska.

In 1905 he joined the faculty of the University of Colorado as Professor of electrical engineering, and from 1918 to 1943 was dean of the College of Engineering.

Active member of state, national and international engineering societies, author of numerous articles in the field of electrical engineering, and a director of the Public Service Company of Colorado.

Consultant for the planning of a proposed municipal light plant at Boulder, 1908-1913; and member of the city council 1918-1922 and 1924-1930.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 88; Minutes of the City Council, 1907-1913, 1918-1930).

### EBEN G. FINE 1865-

A native of Missouri, and deprived of his father in his infancy, he engaged first in farm work and then became an apprentice pharmacist at Hamilton and at Holden, Mo.

In 1885 he came to Boulder to accept employment in Fonda's drugstore, and in 1906-7 he served as second secretary of the Boulder Commercial Association. Subsequently he was manager and president of the Temple Drug Co., and from 1927 to 1936 secretary of the Boulder Chamber of Commerce.

In 1900 he discovered Arapahoe Glacier, and in 1909 he became a charter member of the Rocky Mountain Climbers Club. Also a member of the New Mexico Archeological Society and of the Boulder Chapter of the Archeological Society, and active member of the former Boulder Improvement Society, a director of the Chautauqua Association for forty-five years, and a member of the Episcopal Church.

Member of the city park board, 1908 to 1917, and of the Planning and Parks Commission, 1918 to 1937.

On tours advertising Boulder, he has made more than 3,500 lectures in 28 states. In 1946 he was awarded the University of Colorado Recognition Medal for his services to Boulder and the Rocky Mountain region.

(Boulder Daily Camera, April 25, 1927, March 14, 1931, and Feb. 20, 1946; manuscript "Autobiography" at the Camera office).

### THOMAS H. FITZPATRICK 1852-1935

A native of Pennsylvania, he moved to Kansas in 1868, to Leadville in 1882, to West Plains, Missouri, in 1890, and later to Cheyenne. After years of railroad work he came to Boulder to retire in 1897, and for several years, at the time of the first paving of Boulder's streets, he gave almost full-time volunteer service in the capacity of the chairman of the council committee on streets and alleys.

He was a member of the city council from 1913-1917 and again from 1924-1935. In addition he was an active member of the Masonic Order, of the Congregational Church, of the Boulder Club, and of the Elks lodge.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Oct. 25, 1935; Minutes of the City Council, 1913 to 1935; letter from Jessie Fitzpatrick, June 6, 1946).

### GEORGE F. FONDA 1861-1943

A native of Illinois, he came to Boulder in 1874 to join his brother in the drug business and after 1878 was proprietor of Boulder's leading drugstore. In addition he established a soda water and mineral water plant and later became vice-president of the First National Bank.

He was a high ranking Mason, a member of the Knights of Pythias, the Elks, and A.O.U.W., and vice-president of the First National Bank.

He played in all of Boulder's bands during his years here, was plugman on the champion Boulder Hose and Macky fire company teams, and in 1893 was Democratic candidate for mayor.

After serving a term as alderman, 1886-1887, he was appointed oil inspector, 1890-1891, was elected chief of the volunteer fire department, 1883-1885, 1892-1893, and 1894-1895, and subsequently rendered distinguished service as chief of the combined volunteer and paid fire department, 1899-1902 and 1905 to 1911.

---

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, pages 358-9; Boulder Daily Camera, June 11, 1896, May 8, 1908, and June 19, 1943; Minutes of the City Council, 1883 to 1911.).

### W. A. GRAHAM 1875-1932

A native of Ohio, he came to Boulder from West Virginia in 1904 and established the furniture business of which he was proprietor to the time of his death.

He was an active Presbyterian, a member of the Lions Club, and a director of the Chamber of Commerce.

He was elected to the city council four times, serving from 1911 to 1913, a short term in 1917, and finally from 1926 to the time of his death.

(Boulder Daily Camera, May 31, 1932; Minutes of the City Council, 1911 to 1932).

### OSCAR FITZ-ALLEN GREENE 1843-1899

A native of Maine, he went from school into the Union Army in 1861. After participating in twenty-five major battles of the Civil War, and being wounded twice, he enrolled in Bowdoin College, from which he was graduated in 1869.

~~After a brief stay in Wisconsin, where he was admitted~~  
to the bar, he came to Boulder in 1875. Here he practiced law and became the first professor of Roman law at the University of Colorado.

He was city attorney from 1878 to 1885, 1890 to 1891, and 1892-1896, and was a member of the state general assembly from 1881 to 1883 and of the state senate from 1885 to 1887.

(Byers, Encyclopedia of Biography of Colorado, 1901, page 464; History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 638; and Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, page 637.

### ALFRED A. GREENMAN 1868-1939

A native of Pennsylvania, he came to Boulder in 1890. After employment as a clerk in a book and drug store, he became proprietor of the firm, in 1902, which later established a branch on University Hill and became known as the Greenman Stores.

He was a director and president of the Chautauqua Association for more than thirty-five years and was a founder and president of the Chamber of Commerce.

After serving the city as mayor 1909-1911, he was appointed to the Planning and Parks Commission, in 1924, and continued on it until the time of his death.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 91; Boulder Daily Camera, Oct. 3, 1939; Minutes of the City Council, 1909-1911, 1924-1939).

### LOUIS HERMAN 1868-1934

A native of Germany, he came first to Albany, New York, and then, in 1894, to Boulder, where he engaged in the dry goods business for twenty-six years, until the time of

his death.

He was an active and high ranking Mason, a member and president of the Chamber of Commerce, a member and once grand patriarch of the Odd Fellows, twice president of the Lions Club, a member of the Rebekahs, and Eastern Star, secretary of the Community Hospital Association, a director of the Building and Loan Association, and a director of the Boulder National Bank. Among many community projects he was especially interested in the Day Nursery, the Memorial Gateway, and the Lions Club shelter houses in the mountain parks.

He was thrice elected to the city council, serving from 1918-1920, 1922-1928, and 1930 to 1934, and in 1917 he was a member of the Charter Convention.

(Boulder Daily Camera, July 5, 1934; Minutes of the City Council, 1918 to 1934; letter from Bessie Herman, June 10, 1946).

### DR. HOWARD HULL HEUSTON 1886-

~~A native of Nebraska, he started as a teacher of a country school in Indian Territory (Oklahoma). After a few years as a principal of the high school at Marion, Illinois, and as a superintendent in Oregon, he turned to the study of medicine at the University of Colorado and at Washington University.~~

He has been a practicing physician and surgeon at Boulder since 1919, and is a member of Rotary, the Chamber of

Commerce, and medical societies.

He served the municipality as mayor from 1932 to 1940.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938; page 92; Capitol's Who's Who for Colorado, 1941, page 157; Boulder Daily Camera, Feb. 4, 1932; Minutes of the City Council, 1932-1940).

### GEORGE R. HUBBARD 1902-

A native of Illinois, he came to Boulder in 1922 and was first employed in his father's grocery store.

In 1928-1929 he was employed in the city water and street department, and the next year he worked as a rod man in the department of public service. In 1930 he became city surveyor and since 1932 he has been building inspector and assistant city engineer.

Member of the Masonic lodge and the National Fire Protective Association and past chairman of the Rocky Mountain Chapter of the International Association of Electrical Inspectors.

(Minutes of the City Council, 1932 to 1946; interview, April 17, 1946).

### EMIL A. JOHNSON 1887-

A native of Boulder, Colorado, his life-long career has been the preventing and fighting of fires.

After three years of employment in the city fire department, he became a captian in 1909 and was promoted to

assistant chief in 1912, and since 1916 has been chief of the department.

He is a member and past president of the Missouri Valley Association of Fire Chiefs, and a member of the International Association of Fire Chiefs and the Colorado State Firemen's Association, having been honored with a number of offices in the State Association, and in 1930 helped organize the first State Fire College.

He is a member of the Rotary Club, Chamber of Commerce, and the Masonic and Elks lodges.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 95; Boulder News-Herald, April 3, 1930, and Oct. 20, 1931; Boulder Daily Camera, July 23, 1938, and Oct. 9, 1942.

### RUDOLPH JOHNSON 1883-

A native of Illinois, born at Geneseo, and an alumnus of the Univeristy of Colorado with two degrees, A.B. and L.L.B., he has practiced law at Boulder since 1919. He was an investigator for the Colorado Tax Commission from 1915 to 1919, ~~except for several months service in the United States army.~~

Since 1914 he has been secretary of the Colorado State Grange. He is a member of the American Legion, Disabled American Veterans, Boulder Chamber of Commerce, and Congregational Church. He also belongs to various lodges, numerous state organizations, and many national legal and welfare societies.

He was elected to the House of Representatives of Colorado four times on the Republican ticket, once on the Democratic ticket, and was elected in 1936 to the State Senate on the Democratic ticket. In 1928 he was a candidate for Attorney General of the State of Colorado. From 1929 to 1941 he was Director of Public Welfare of the City of Boulder.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 95; Minutes of the City Council, 1929-1941; letter of May 28, 1946).

### H. C. McCLINTOCK 1902-

A native of Pennsylvania, he was educated in the Denver public schools and at Colorado State College. After three years with the Wyoming state highway department he came to Boulder in 1926 to accept employment as city building inspector. From 1928 to 1930 he was building inspector and assistant city engineer, since 1930 he has been director of public service, and since 1932 he has held the combined offices of director of public service and city manager.

In addition, from 1941 to 1945 he served ex officio as coordinator of the Boulder Civilian Defense Council, and in 1942 he investigated needs for critical materials as a consultant for the War Production Board.

Member of the Chamber of Commerce, member and past president of Kiwanis, past lieutenant-governor of the Rocky Mountain District Kiwanis International, member of the Masons

and past master of the Blue Lodge, elder and thrice chairman of the board of the Christian church, past president and vice-president of the Colorado Municipal League, member of the International Association of City Managers, past chairman of the Rocky Mountain Section of the American Water Works Association and past chairman of the Rocky Mountain Sewage Works Association. Awarded the distinguished service key by the Boulder Junior Chamber of Commerce in 1935.

(Capitol's Who's Who for Colorado, 1941, page 246; Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 99; Minutes of the City Council, 1928 to 1946; Boulder News-Herald, May 1, 1926; Boulder Daily Camera, Feb. 24, 1930; Dec. 10, 1931; June 8, 1932; Oct. 12, 1933; June 6, 1934; Jan. 23, 1935; Dec. 11, 1941; Sept. 14 and 28, 1942; and June 12, 1944).

### FLORA S. McHARG 1873-

A native of Illinois, Flora E. Silliman was admitted to the bar in Colorado and was graduated from the Law School at the University of Colorado in 1901. That same year she was married to Thomas A. McHarg, Boulder attorney.

Mrs. McHarg did not practice law, but instead made extensive use of her legal training for the benefit of many civic enterprises. She has been an active member of the Chamber of Commerce, American Association of University Women, Daughters of the American Revolution, Presbyterian Church, Phi Delta Delta, Woman's Club, the board of the local Red Cross chapter, and the board of the former University Hospital. In addition she helped found the Community

Hospital Association, the Visiting Nurse Association, the Day Nursery, and the Colorado Conference of Social Work, and is a past president of the Woman's Club, the Fortnightly Club, and the Colorado Federation of Women's Clubs.

In 1907 she was appointed to membership on the first city park board, on which she served continuously through 1917, and afterwards, from 1918 to 1920, on the reorganized Planning and Parks Commission. In 1917, as one of two women delegates in the Charter Convention, she successfully advocated the adoption of the Hare system, served as chairman of the committee on parks and a member of the committee on public health, and then served on the legal committee which put the Charter in its final form. Later, in 1920, she was the second woman to be elected to the city council, and her term ended in 1926.

(Baker, History of Colorado, pages 489-90; Minutes of the City Council, 1907-1926; letter of April 24, 1946).

### ANDREW J. MACKY 1834-1907

A native of New York, he first worked as a carpenter in that state and in Wisconsin, and then came to California Gulch, Colorado, during the gold rush in 1859. He located at Boulder in 1860, where he built the first frame house and the first brick store building, the latter in partnership with Charles Dabney.

From 1861 to 1870 he was Boulder's second postmaster

and from 1863 to 1872 the second county treasurer. Subsequently he became the city's leading insurance broker, an investor in real estate development, and president of the First National Bank (after 1885).

In addition he served as clerk of the District Court from 1870 to 1878, as city clerk from 1872 to 1878, as city treasurer from 1878 to 1885, as secretary of School District No. 3, as secretary of the Boulder County Industrial Association, as secretary of the Boulder County Pioneers, as treasurer of the Board of Trade, as president of the Macky Hose Company, and as president of the Federal Gas Co.

He was a charter member of the Elks lodge and a benefactor of that lodge and many other community enterprises. In his will he provided for the building of the auditorium at the University.

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, pages 375-6; History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, pages 661-2; Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1861 to 1872, Minutes of the Town Board and City Council, 1872 to 1885; Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 10, 1906; June 11, 1907; Nov. 24, 1909; and April 22, 1926; and numerous items in earlier newspapers).

### ARTHUR F. MASTERS 1890-

A native of Kansas, he engaged in farming except 1918-19, when he served in the United States Navy during the first World War.

Soon after locating at Boulder, in 1923, he joined the city police force, with which he has since been connected.

Member of the American Legion, Methodist church, and Chamber of Commerce, and vice-president of the Colorado Police Protective Association.

Police officer, 1923-1927, assistant chief, 1927-1929, captain, 1929 to 1939, and police chief since 1939.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Sept. 23, 1939; Minutes of the City Council since 1939, and interview, April 16, 1946).

### JAMES P. MAXWELL 1839-1929

A native of Wisconsin and a graduate of Lawrence University at Appleton, he came to Central City, Colorado, in 1860 and engaged in mining and the lumber business there until 1868. Then he moved to Boulder to operate a saw mill and soon afterward turned to surveying and politics.

From 1872 to 1874 he served a term in the territorial legislature, and from 1876 to 1880 in the state senate, to which he was returned in 1896. He was elected a town trustee in 1871 and again in 1874, followed by one term as mayor, 1878 to 1879, and a term as county treasurer, 1880 to 1882. In addition he was city engineer from 1883 to 1889, and in those years he also directed government surveys in western Colorado. After four years as state engineer, 1889 to 1893, he returned to his former post as city engineer, 1899 to 1907, during the early development of Boulder's mountain water system. From 1910 to the time of his death he was president and then chairman of the board of the First

National Bank.

In addition he helped build the Silver Lake Ditch, and founded the town of Steamboat Springs.

He was a Scottish Rite Mason and a state commander of the Knights Templar.

(Hall, History of the State of Colorado, IV, 1889-95, pages 521-2; Baker, History of Colorado, V, 1927, pages 710-13; Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, page 319; History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, page 660; Minutes of the Town and City Council, 1871 to 1907; Boulder Daily Camera, November 24, 1909; and numerous items in earlier newspapers).

### SCOTT MITCHELL 1873-

A native of Kansas City, Missouri, he has been a railroad contractor most of his life, first with his father's firm, then as vice-president of the L. J. Smith Construction Co. of Kansas City, and finally, from 1926 to 1934, as president of the Clinch-Mitchell Construction Co. of Chicago and Kansas City.

He became a resident of Boulder in 1907 and served as city manager from 1920 through 1925, during the critical testing years of the city manager form of government.

He was for a long time a member of the Boulder Club, Rotary, and Masonic order.

(Minutes of the City Council, 1920-1925; interview April 19, 1946).

### FRANK L. MOORHEAD 1885-

A native of Boulder and an alumnus of the University of Colorado, he has been practicing law at Boulder since 1910.

He is a member of the Chamber of Commerce and of the Kiwanis Club, a past president of the County Bar Association, and also of the city attorney's section of the Colorado Municipal League.

In addition to serving as city attorney since 1916, he has been acting city manager, 1925 to 1928, and for brief periods in 1918 and 1932.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 100; Minutes of the City Council, 1918 to 1946; Boulder Daily Camera, April 1, 1940, and May 12, 1941).

### DR. HENRY L. MORENCY 1896-

A native of Detroit, Michigan, he was graduated from the University of Notre Dame and from Colorado Agricultural College, and had advanced work at the University of California, specializing in biology and in public health.

From 1925 to 1926 he was instructor in physiology at the Michigan State College, from 1926 to 1927 in the extension service at Colorado State College, and from 1927 to 1929 assistant professor of bacteriology and pathology at that institution. From 1929 to 1932 he was associated with the Boulder health department, and since 1932, director of public health for the city of Boulder.

He is a member of Rotary and of several local and state medical societies and national scientific societies.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 100; Capitol's Who's Who for Colorado, 1941, page 271; Minutes of the City Council, 1932-1946).

### JOHN J. MORSE 1867-1934

A native of New York state, he came to Boulder in 1909 after extensive experience in mining. In 1913 he became an employe of the city, and from 1922 to the time of his death he was superintendent of the city water system.

(Boulder Daily Camera, Dec. 17, 1934).

### EPHRAIM POUND 1817-1892

A native of New York, he moved first to Kansas, and then to Colorado in 1862. He located at Boulder soon afterward and lived here until 1885.

In the 1860's he was proprietor of the Colorado House, and county sheriff. After one term on the board of town trustees, 1872-3, he was elected mayor three times in succession, 1873-6. During his administration the town built its first water works system, of which he served as commissioner from 1875 to 1877.

(Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1862-1871; Minutes of the Town Board, 1872-1877; Boulder Daily Camera, April 5, 1892).

### ROLLA C. PRATER 1883-

A native of Kentucky and a graduate of the business college at Springfield, Missouri, and of the normal school at Alva, Oklahoma, he came to Colorado in 1911. After three years in the lumber business he became a forest ranger in Holy Cross National Forest (1914-1922), and then for three years was with the South Park Gold Dredging Co.

He joined the Boulder police department in 1925, and from 1927 to 1939 was chief of police. Since then he has had government employment in Oregon.

At Boulder he was a Mason, a Knight Templar, a Presbyterian, a president of the Colorado Rifle Association and president of the Colorado Police Protective Association.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 104; Minutes of the City Council, 1927-1939; Boulder News-Herald, March 29, 1927).

### HENRY M. SAYRE 1883-

A native of Ohio, and a graduate of the business college at Wheeling, West Virginia, he came to Boulder in 1907 to teach commerce in the high school until 1924, and in that time he also was an instructor of accounting at the University for ten years.

Since 1924 he has been with the National State Bank, as cashier to 1935 and since then, vice-president and cashier.

He is a member of the Methodist church and of the

Colorado Society of Certified Public Accountants, and is a past president of the Boulder Chamber of Commerce.

Since 1917 he has been city auditor, and in addition he served six years on the city school board, from 1925 to 1931.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 105; Capitol's Who's Who for Colorado, 1941, page 342; Minutes of the City Council, 1918 to 1946; Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 8, 1941).

### HERBERT M. SPENCER 1888-

A native of Pennsylvania, he came to Colorado in 1918 and five years later opened the Spencer-Morris candy store at Boulder.

Since 1934 he has been a justice of the peace and city police magistrate, and in this office he introduced the "one free ticket" system for minor offenders.

He is a member of the Chamber of Commerce and Elks lodge, and in the Masonic order he has been twice master and since 1933 secretary of Lodge No. 45.

(Minutes of the City Council, 1934 to 1946; interview, April 18, 1946).

### FREDERICK A. SQUIRES 1819-1893

A native of Massachusetts, he first worked at the tinner's trade, until 1856, when he became proprietor of a hotel at Geneseo, Illinois.

He came to Boulder in 1860, where he first operated a

hotel and next, from 1866 to 1871, a lumber and mercantile establishment, both in partnership with J. A. Tourtellot. After 1871 he continued as sole proprietor in the mercantile business and also operated gold mines at Gold Hill.

He was active in county politics and in the Boulder County Pioneers, and sponsored numerous community enterprises. In 1871 the county commissioners appointed him one of the first trustees of the Town of Boulder.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, pages 681-2; Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 4, 1893; Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1861 to 1871; and numerous early newspaper items).

### MARINUS G. SMITH 1819-1901

A native of New York state, his first employment was in a tin shop, after which he became proprietor of a hardware store and then the operator of a mail and stage line. After a year's service in the Mexican war, he went to California, where he engaged in the cattle business and in mining until he located in Illinois in 1851. During the next eight years he was a farmer and later a grain commissioner.

In 1859 he migrated to Boulder, where he operated an express and mail service until 1871. In addition he acquired lands in Boulder Valley, some of which became part of the townsite in 1871, and much of the remainder was admitted as additions to the city later. He also donated part of the original site for the University.

During the Indian strife of 1863-4, he was commissioned captain of the home guards, and in the 1860's he served as county commissioner. In 1871 the board of commissioners appointed him one of the first trustees of the Town of Boulder.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, pages 679-680; Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1861 to 1871; Boulder Daily Camera, Jan. 12, 1901).

### GEORGE W. TEAL 1863-1932

A native of Manchester, England, in 1872 he came to Georgetown, Colorado, where his father was superintendent of a mine. He returned to Cornwall to study mining and completed his studies at Freiberg, where he was graduated in 1883.

In 1887, when he was appointed U. S. deputy mineral and land surveyor, he established his office at Boulder, and in addition he was engaged as a mining engineer and at times as superintendent of large mining interests in Boulder County.

He was a member of Rotary, of the Elks lodge, and of the Episcopal church, and was a Mason of high rank.

He was county surveyor from 1891 to 1901 and city engineer from 1892 to 1899.

After serving a short term as alderman, in 1917, and as a member of the Planning and Parks Commission, 1918-21, he was appointed city manager in 1928, which position he filled until the time of his death.

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898, pages 753-4; Minutes of the City Council, 1890 to 1932; Boulder Daily Camera, Dec. 7, 1928, and May 31, 1932).

### FRANK W. THURMAN 1888-

A native of Missouri, he located in Colorado first at Louisville, where he was agent for the Colorado and Southern Railway, 1906-1917. From 1917 to 1925 he was secretary-treasurer of the Cracker Jack Coal Co., since 1926 he has been manager of the Black Diamond Fuel Co., and since 1934 a director and then secretary of the Imperial Coal Co., Denver.

He is a member and past president and secretary of the Lions Club, an ex-ruler of the Elks lodge, a director of the Chamber of Commerce, a member of the Country Club, secretary of the Community Hospital Association, a director of the Chautauqua Association, and a member of the board of the Methodist church.

In 1934 he was appointed to the city council and two years later he was elected for a six-year term, followed by reelection in 1942. Since 1940 he has been mayor, and during the second World War he was chairman of the Boulder Civilian

Defense Committee and chairman of the United Service Organizations.

(Who's Who in Colorado, 1938, page 108; Capitol's Who's Who for Colorado, 1941, page 392; Minutes of the City Council, 1935 to 1946; Boulder Daily Camera, August 8, 1934; biographical data, letter of June 11, 1946).

### MONTFORD S. WHITELEY 1860-1933

A native of Georgia, he came to Colorado in 1877 and enrolled in the University. Three years later he opened a real estate office at Boulder and in 1882 he became an employe in a hardware and grocery store. In 1897 he bought the hardware department, which he expanded subsequently into one of Boulder's leading business establishments.

He was a Woodman, and a director of the Building and Loan Association. After having been president of the school board for two terms, he was elected alderman in 1887 (to 1889), and from 1899 to 1905 he served three terms as mayor.

(Portrait and Biographical Record of Denver and Vicinity, 1898; pages 741-2; Minutes of the City Council, 1887 to 1905; Boulder County Herald, May 3, 1882; Boulder Daily Camera, April 3, 1901, and July 13, 1933).

### ALPHEUS WRIGHT 1832-1901

A native of New York state, he taught school in order to finance his education in the Canton and Potsdam academies. In 1853 he went to Australia during the gold excitement there, but returned to the United States to take up teaching

and further study, first in New York state and then in Wisconsin. He became county clerk and justice of the peace at Prairie du Chien, where he was admitted to the bar in 1857.

In 1859 he came to Colorado, and after four years in Gilpin County, located at Boulder, where he practiced law and pursued his profitable mining interests.

In 1865 he was elected to the territorial legislature, and in 1867 he became county attorney. Later he served in the state legislature (elected 1883), and afterwards he was county judge.

In the meantime the county commissioners had appointed him one of the original trustees of the town of Boulder, in 1871, to which office he was also elected in 1874 for a one-year term. He was city engineer from 1873 to 1874, city attorney in 1874, and from 1884 to 1885 he served the city as mayor for one term.

He was a popular orator for all occasions, and in politics he was quite independent, accepting nominations from time to time on Democratic, Republican, Greenback, Citizens, and Populist tickets.

(History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys, 1880, pages 699-700; Bancroft, History of Nevada, Colorado, and Wyoming, 1890, page 576; Minutes of the County Commissioners, 1865 to 1871; Minutes of the Town Board and City Council, 1871 to 1885; and numerous items in the newspapers).

## BOULDER BIBLIOGRAPHY

Materials available locally, with library or office where available indicated parenthetically, employing these abbreviations:

- CO ---- City offices
- BCO ---- Boulder County Offices
- BPL ---- Boulder Public Library
- DCL ---- Daily Camera Library
- UCGL --- University of Colorado General Library
- UCHC --- University of Colorado Historical Collections

Since much material for the future museum is stored at the Daily Camera office, no effort has been made here to differentiate between those items which are in the Camera Library and those which will be moved later to the museum.

For convenience all sources are included in one alphabetical list.

Adriance, Rev. Jacob, Ames, Nebraska. Letter of April 14, 1904, to the Rev. John A. Davis, Boulder (UCHC).

Alden, C. L. Study of Boulder School Children. University of Colorado thesis, 1907 (UCGL).

Allen, H. W. Early History of Masonry in Northern Colorado. Columbia Lodge No. 14, 1907, manuscript (office of H. O. Andrew).

American City, magazine, 1909-1946 (UCGL).

Andrew, Henry O., Fonda, George F., and Thomas, Tudor A. Mt. Sinai Commandery No. 7, Knights Templar, Boulder, Colorado..., History, Semicentennial, 1881 (U.D.) to 1931, inclusive. Manuscript (office of H. O. Andrew).

"Attacks against P. R. Repulsed in Hamilton and Boulder,"  
National Municipal Review, Dec., 1933, 22:613-14 (UCGL).

Baggs, M. L. Colorado, the Queen Jewel of the Rockies.  
Boston: Page, 1918 (UCGL).

Baker, J. H., and Hafen, L. R., editors. History of Colorado, five volumes. Denver: Linderman, 1927 (UCGL, UCHC, PL, DCL).

Bancroft, H. H. History of Nevada, Colorado and Wyoming, 1540-1888. San Francisco History Co., 1890 (UCGL, PL).

Barrett, H. M. "Education in Colorado" in Colorado, Short Studies of Its Past and Present. Boulder: University, 1927 (UCGL, PL).

Beardsley, I. H. Echoes from Peak and Plain. Cincinnati: Curts and Jennings, 1898 (UCHC).

Bensel's Boulder County Directory. Trinidad, Colorado: Bensel Directory Co., 1892 (DCL).

Bishop, Isabella Lucy (Bird). A Lady's Life in the Rocky Mountains. London: Murray, 1910 (UCGL).

Bishop, L. E. Investigation of Sewage Disposal at Boulder, Colorado. University thesis, 1908 (UCGL).

Bixby, Amos. "History of Boulder County," in History of Clear Creek and Boulder Valleys. Chicago: Baskin and Co., 1880 (UCGL, PL, DCL).

Blackmore, William. Colorado: Its Resources, Parks and Prospects as a New Field for Emigration. London: Low, 1869 (UCGL).

Bliss, F. V. O., and Curtis, E. C. Preliminary Estimate for a Hydroelectric Plant at Boulder Settling Basin. University thesis, 1907 (UCGL).
